Breast cancer is the most frequently diagnosed cancer and the most frequent cause of
cancer-related deaths in women worldwide. It affects women both in the developed and the
developing world. As per WHO, breast cancer accounts for 2.09 million cases and 627000
deaths globally.
 The program is directed towards highlighting the gravity of this disease, raising awareness about its early diagnosis, and breaking the existing stigma surrounding it. 

In addition to this, signed certificates on behalf of Techfest, IIT Bombay will be provided to every participant who attends the entire workshop, as a token of your solidarity with the initiative.

Time-3:00P.M-4:00 P.M

11/13/21, 10:21â€¯PM - Ishita Pandey: The NEO Educational Foundation presents to you 
*The 5th National Engineering Olympiad*!

The National Engineering Olympiad is a competitive platform for the engineering students to showcase your aptitude skills and represent yourself at the national level.

Register now!
https://nationalolympiad.org/?refid=234831311

*The Rounds:*
Similar to the previous four editions of the National Engineering Olympiad, the exam will be conducted in two rounds.

Round 1: Basic Aptitude Test- 60 mins, 60 questions. 
Dates are 24th & 25th November 2021. 
Round 2: Technical Ability Test- Online MCQ Exam based on your syllabus of the year & branch you are studying in. 

*Please Note:*
Both rounds are to be attempted _online_ from your home!

*The Rewards:* 

_For the top performers:_
-Top 10 of each year & branch will be awarded a Medal of Excellence.
-Top 30 of each year & branch will be awarded a Certificate of Excellence.

_For all participants:_
-Guaranteed Internships in various domains.
-A national-level participation certificate.
-Career-oriented webinars by experts for free.

(More details are available on the website)

Hurry up! Registrations have started!
Visit https://nationalolympiad.org/?refid=234831311

*The 5th National Engineering Olympiad*!

The National Engineering Olympiad is a competitive platform for the engineering students to showcase your aptitude skills and represent yourself at the national level.

Register now!
https://nationalolympiad.org/?refid=276021711

*The Rounds:*
Similar to the previous four editions of the National Engineering Olympiad, the exam will be conducted in two rounds.

Round 1: Basic Aptitude Test- 60 mins, 60 questions. 
Dates are 24th & 25th November 2021. 
Round 2: Technical Ability Test- Online MCQ Exam based on your syllabus of the year & branch you are studying in. 

*Please Note:*
Both rounds are to be attempted _online_ from your home!

*The Rewards:* 

_For the top performers:_
-Top 10 of each year & branch will be awarded a Medal of Excellence.
-Top 30 of each year & branch will be awarded a Certificate of Excellence.

_For all participants:_
-Guaranteed Internships in various domains.
-A national-level participation certificate.
-Career-oriented webinars by experts for free.

(More details are available on the website)

Hurry up! Registrations have started!
Visit https://nationalolympiad.org/?refid=276021711

    if (len(str1)!=len(str2)):
        print ("The strings are not anagrams of each other.")
    else:
        num = 0
        for i in range(0,len(str1)):
            for j in range(0,len(str2)):
                if (sorted(str1)==sorted(str2)):
                    num = 1
    if (num==1):
        print ("The strings are anagrams of each other.")
    else:
        print ("The strings are anagrams of each other.")

    if (num==1):
        return 1
    else:
        return num*factorial(num-1)

    if (sum(list)==num):

12/14/21, 10:12â€¯PM - +91 97111 20216: class py_solution:
    def int_to_Roman(self, num):
        val = [
            1000, 900, 500, 400,
            100, 90, 50, 40,
            10, 9, 5, 4,
            1
            ]
        syb = [
            "M", "CM", "D", "CD",
            "C", "XC", "L", "XL",
            "X", "IX", "V", "IV",
            "I"
            ]
        roman_num = ''
        i = 0
        while  num > 0:
            for _ in range(num // val[i]):
                roman_num += syb[i]
                num -= val[i]
            i += 1
        return roman_num


num1=1
num2=4000
print('Converting ',num1,' to roman')
print('roman equivalent of ',num1,' is =' ,py_solution().int_to_Roman(num1))
print('Converting ',num2,' to roman')
print('roman equivalent of ',num2,' is =' ,py_solution().int_to_Roman(num2))

12/14/21, 10:12â€¯PM - +91 97111 20216: class py_solution:
 def threeSum(self, nums):
        nums, result, i = sorted(nums), [], 0
        while i < len(nums) - 2:
            j, k = i + 1, len(nums) - 1
            while j < k:
                if nums[i] + nums[j] + nums[k] < 0:
                    j += 1
                elif nums[i] + nums[j] + nums[k] > 0:
                    k -= 1
                else:
                    result.append([nums[i] , nums[j] , nums[k]])
                    j, k = j + 1, k - 1
                    while j < k and nums[j] == nums[j - 1] :
                        j += 1
                    while j < k and nums[k] == nums[k + 1] :
                        k -= 1
            i += 1
            while i < len(nums) - 2 and nums[i] == nums[i - 1] :
                i += 1
        return result

lst1 = [-25, -10, -7, -3, 2, 4, 8, 10]
print("Given list is =",lst1)
print("Output is :")
print(py_solution().threeSum(lst1))

class Bus(Vehicle):

        fare_car = self.capacity * 100 
        total_fare = fare_car + (0.1 *fare_car)
        return total_fare

central part of intonation.

just mean to say. Here the pitch of the voice says a lot.

sentence can be said in different ways, which would indicate whether
the speaker is angry, happy, grateful or just indifferent.

3/25/22, 3:00â€¯PM - Siddharth Singh CS Ds ğŸŒ¹: My dear Students 
CS-DS 3rd Sem 2022.

Today, I felt writing to you the experience I had with you all this long historical semester. You are going to remember this semester, so will I. Time, those who have mastered this word shall know and will understand, if not now, is the greatest dictator. 
Well, I had a rich experience with you all. Though Technical communication as a subject was boring to you all by the fact of your ignorance, perhaps, that â€¦â€™whatâ€™s there to learn about?â€™. Yes, we all have mastered a language before prep school and you hv been using it till date. 
My students, I hope this reflection of yours about language today shall change with time as you progress for sure. However, I would like to advice you for the last time that not to be too late. 

Your thoughts must keep wondering and rememberâ€¦.wonderful thoughts finds itâ€™s shape through language only. 
Do not waste your life wandering, for this shall keep your mind always confused and stressed. 

Some of you dared to attend near about 50 classes which I heartily appreciate though it was little tasking for you as well as me. 

Some left halfway and some were invisible. Though this semester you had both on campus and online mode, some of you attended the classes with self integrity while others took their studies too casually specially communication paper. 
More so thanks  to technology that you had got the liberty to hid behind giving excuses. 

Now as your exams are about to be over, I request each one of you to take some time to contemplate why you were born in this world as human beings, what is your purpose of life and what you dream and what you want to do before you bid adieu to this beautiful world. 
Each of you has the potential and talent. I could see that most of you had prepared the mini dissertation assignment simply by copying others work and establishing the work as yours so calmly. 
Today what you did will turn out to be a big hurdle in your lifeâ€¦.. and shall be severely impaired not knowing how to express your ideas. I pray that you would stop such habits and be honest to yourself. 
We know we are never going to be in this mode (teacher-student) for the rest of our life. But wherever you are and whatever you do, try to polish your use of language with whosoever you get to interact professionally and personally as well. Never take language for granted as language, once spoken, never has a reverse gear. Use it mindfully. And yes, a good mind delivers good communication. 
Hope my association with you and my teachings show the light in your life. 
If I continue to be a faculty here in GCET, you are always welcome to meet me. I shall try my best to help you. 
Good luck and God bless you

Dr K. Dey.

In a small town called Savner in Nagpur, Maharashtra, there live a little girl named Dhanashree Chakole. She is only five years old, with big bright eyes and a smile that could light up a room. Her mother was her world, her everything. But tragedy struck when her mother took her own life in 2022, leaving Dhanashree behind.
Despite the pain and heartache, Dhanashree's aunt stepped up to take care of her. However, the responsibility of raising a child and providing for her education and living expenses can be challenging, especially for someone who is financially unstable.
That's where Suvidha comes in. Suvidha is raising funds for Dhanashree's education and living expenses, to ensure that this little girl has a bright future ahead of her. Suvidha understands that education is the key to unlocking opportunities and breaking the cycle of poverty. By donating to Dhanashree's cause, you can make a meaningful difference in her life.
Imagine the impact that your donation could have on Dhanashree's life. With your help, she can have access to quality education, proper healthcare, and basic necessities that every child deserves. Your donation can give Dhanashree hope, a sense of security, and a chance to dream big.
So please, come forward and donate whatever you can to help Dhanashree's cause. Even the smallest donation can make a big difference. Spread the word and encourage your friends and family to do the same. Together, we can make a positive impact in the world, one child at a time.
For those who are interested in making a larger donation and would like to learn more about how they can support Dhanashree's cause, please don't hesitate to contact Suvidha.
